Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters Commemorative Week 119

Ye Chucang Talks About Sports

Both Serious and Humorous, the Audience Chuckles

Yesterday (7th), the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters held an expanded commemorative week. Following speeches by Dai Jitao and He Yingqin, Ye Chucang spoke at length about sports. The following is a record of his speech: "These days, it's okay not to mention Hangzhou, but once you mention Hangzhou, you have to talk about the National Games, how bustling and lively they are. Twenty years ago, I was also an athlete. At that time, the high jump used two boards with a stick placed on them. According to the level of English, there were three groups competing. As a result, Group A won, and Group B didn't even smile at them for three weeks. At that time, promoting sports actually caused a lot of negative feelings. In this conference, the newspaper records say that a certain province is better than another province, and a certain province is not as good as another province, which is not good. The province is just an organizational name, which is convenient for administration. It does not divide the people of the country into several boundaries. This conference is not a competition between one person and another, nor is it a competition between one province and another. The purpose is to create new records and hope that the next conference will be better than the previous one. This is an important meaning. I remember Mr. Dai once said in a speech that people are old when they reach fifty. This sentence means that the physical fitness of the current people is not as good as that of the predecessors, because the ancients were considered old at seventy or eighty. If this continues, maybe they will be called Liaohus basketball battle Wang Kai photography

Old at thirty, so the purpose of this conference is to hope that the physical fitness of the people and the physical fitness of the nation will be strengthened due to the promotion of the conference. "When Ye spoke, he was both serious and humorous, which made the audience very interested and smiled from time to time.

Full Program of the National Education Conference

The Conference is Scheduled to Be Held on the 15th of This Month

Yesterday, the Preparatory Committee telegraphed to hold the conference on time and not postpone it. As for the agenda, participants could propose it at will last time. During the meeting, it will be discussed. This newspaper has published several sections, but there have been revisions. Now the full program will be disclosed day by day.

Hubei Female Instructor (Right) Ms. Yang Wenmin (Left) Ms. He Xuchu Wang Kai Photography

Explanation of the National Education Improvement Program 135

(1) The guiding principles for the compilation of this program are: For compulsory education and adult literacy supplementary education, the focus is on popularization within a limited time; for secondary education, the focus is not on rapid promotion, but on qualitative improvement first, and high schools should especially adopt a centralized approach; for higher education, the focus is on consolidation and improvement, rather than increasing the number; other social education, overseas Chinese education, and Mongolian-Tibetan education should take into account needs and national financial resources, compromise and average, and strive to be appropriate and practical.

(2) This program is divided into ten chapters, and the main items are as follows:

Chapter 1 Preliminary Plan for Implementing Compulsory Education

Chapter 2 Preliminary Plan for Implementing Adult Supplementary Education

Chapter 3 Plan for Establishing Teacher Training Institutions at All Levels and Types

Chapter 4 Plan for Improving Elementary Education

Chapter 5 Plan for Improving Secondary Education

Chapter 6 Plan for Improving Higher Education

Chapter 7 Plan for Improving Social Education

Chapter 8 Plan for Improving Overseas Chinese Education

Chapter 9 Plan for Implementing Mongolian-Tibetan Education

Chapter 10 Total Budget for the Whole Program

(3) Unless otherwise specified in the text regarding special cities, other matters not specified shall be handled in accordance with the methods for each province in the text. (4) In the total budget, in addition to the central government expenditures, only the total amounts for each province and each county and city are listed each year. During implementation, each province and each county and city should determine the annual budget for each provincial government and each county and city separately, taking into account the circumstances.

(5) This program only lists the budget, and there are no plans for raising funds, because the source of funds is a financial program, which should be calculated by the financial authorities after the education program is decided, and a separate plan should be formulated for implementation.

Preliminary Plan for Implementing Compulsory Education, Chapter 1 136

(1) Goals

The goal of this plan is to provide four years of primary education to all school-age children nationwide. However, for poor children in rural or urban areas, adjustments (Note 1) or shortening (Note 2) of their schooling period may be considered, with supplementary schools (Note 3) or a "self-study system" (Note 4) to supplement their required compulsory education.

(2) Timeframe

It is planned to complete the establishment of national teacher training institutions within five years, and at the same time, to initiate 1,500 compulsory education experimental zones in urban and rural areas (Note 5), so that all important counties across the country can begin small-scale experiments in compulsory education. Subsequently, it will be promoted year by year, and by the end of the twentieth year, a uniform four-year compulsory education will be implemented nationwide.

(3) Problems that Urgently Need to Be Solved

A. How to ensure that all school-age children nationwide enroll in school. To implement four years of compulsory education, based on a ratio of one-tenth of the population, there should be 43 million school-age children nationwide (Note 6). Excluding the students who are already enrolled in school (Note 7), there are still 37 million people without the opportunity to receive education. In addition, with the natural population increase over the next twenty years, the number of school-age children will increase by at least 3 million, totaling 40 million people. Of these 40 million school-age children, according to the distribution of urban and rural populations, urban areas account for about 15 percent, and rural areas account for about 85 percent. The primary problem at present is how to ensure that all 40 million children enroll in school.

B. How to train the required teachers. Assuming that each teacher is responsible for educating an average of 40 students (Note 8), then the country needs to increase the number of teachers by one million. However, teachers cannot serve in primary schools for life. Assuming that one-fifth are replaced every five years, then eight-tenths of the teachers will be replaced in twenty years. At the beginning, the number of teachers is too small, and the length of service cannot but be extended. Assuming that the number of replacements is reduced by half, then among the one million teachers, 400,000 will be replaced in twenty years. Therefore, 1.4 million teachers must be trained in twenty years to meet the need. The second problem that urgently needs to be solved at present is how to train 1.4 million teachers in twenty years.

C. How to increase the required school buildings and equipment in the classrooms. Assuming that each classroom can accommodate about 40 people (Note 9), then the country needs to add one million classrooms and one million sets of classroom equipment. Some people suggest that schools adopt the Gray System, with each classroom accommodating two classes of students, which would reduce the number of classrooms. However, in reality, the Gray System can only be implemented in industrialized and commercially developed cities with concentrated populations. If the Gray System is used in sparsely populated rural areas with inconvenient transportation, it would reduce the number of students in each class, not only failing to save classrooms but also increasing the number of teachers, which would be uneconomical. The number of students in cities only accounts for 15 percent of the total. Even if all primary schools in cities adopt the Gray System, it would only reduce the number of classrooms by about 7 percent. However, after the Gray System is implemented, school classrooms can no longer be used to conduct adult supplementary education, making it difficult to serve as a center for social reform (Social Center). Therefore, saving 7 percent of the classrooms is actually a loss. Therefore, this plan still intends to add one million classrooms. However, how to raise huge sums of money to build so many classrooms and add the necessary equipment in the classrooms is the third problem that urgently needs to be solved at present.

D. How to raise the required funds. For each child enrolled in school, the government

must bear at least seven yuan per year (Note 10). To enroll 40 million children, the annual expenditure needs to be increased by 280 million yuan, excluding the money needed to build classrooms and train teachers (Note 11). How to raise this large sum of money and how the central and local governments should share the cost of compulsory education are the most important problems that need to be solved at present.

(4) Methods of Training Teachers and Enrolling Students in Stages

First, of the 1.4 million teachers needed to implement compulsory education, 15 percent will serve in urban primary schools, about 200,000 people. They can be trained by existing normal schools and normal departments of high schools in cities. The remaining 85 percent will serve in rural primary schools, about 1.2 million people. They should be trained by rural normal schools established in each county.

Second, the teachers of urban normal schools will be trained by existing normal universities or education schools of various universities, as well as colleges and specialized departments within universities that are related to teacher training.

Third, the teachers of county-level rural normal schools will be trained by provincial-level rural normal colleges and rural normal specialized departments (hereinafter referred to as specialized departments).

Fourth, the teachers of provincial-level rural normal colleges and specialized departments will be trained by the National Compulsory Education College.

North Beiping Men's Basketball Team, photo by Wang Kai

Fifth, county-level rural normal schools will be established separately in large counties or jointly in upper-level counties. A total of 1,500 schools will be fully established within five years. The 1.2 million rural primary school teachers needed will be trained by these 1,500 normal schools. On average, each school must train 800 teachers. From the sixth year onwards, each school should have an average of 53 graduates per year. These normal schools recruit graduates from higher primary schools and train them for three years (this is the minimum, see Article 11). During these three years, there will inevitably be many dropouts. Approximately 120 students are needed to produce 53 graduates to serve as rural primary school teachers. As a transitional measure at present, private school teachers should be recruited and trained to meet the immediate needs. On average, 200 people should be trained each year by the county-level rural normal schools.

Sixth, each county-level rural normal school should train 120 students at a time and have at least 10 teachers. The 1,500 normal schools will need a total of 15,000 teachers. Among these 15,000 people, one-fifth will be replaced every five years, accounting for six-tenths in fifteen years. However, since not many schools will be established at the beginning, the number of teachers replaced can also be reduced. Therefore, in fifteen years, only about four-tenths of the teachers will actually need to be replaced. To supplement these replaced teachers, 6,000 more teachers must be trained, totaling 21,000 people, to ensure that the county-level normal schools do not feel a shortage of teachers.

Seventh, to train these 21,000 people, 27 rural normal schools and specialized departments must be specially established in various provinces, each training an average of 777 people. Among them, 15,000 people must be successfully trained before the end of the fourth year so that the county-level normal schools in various provinces can be fully established at the beginning of the fifth year. From the second year to the fourth year, 5,000 people must be trained each year. Each of the 27 provinces must train an average of 180 people each year, totaling 540 people in three years.

Eighth, the 540 teachers needed for provincial-level rural normal colleges and specialized departments will be trained by the National Compulsory Education College, training 270 people each year for two years. Afterwards, 100 people must continue to be trained each year to fill vacancies and improve their level.

Ninth, the National Compulsory Education College and experimental zones will be established in the first year. First, university graduates will be recruited and trained for one year, and then they will be assigned to various provinces to serve as teachers in rural normal colleges and rural normal specialized departments. They can also serve as compulsory education administrators in various provinces. The central compulsory education experimental zones should be divided into two locations, one in the city and one in the countryside, for the students of the college to conduct field experiments and serve as the foundation for promoting compulsory education nationwide.

Tenth, the rural normal colleges and rural normal specialized departments specially established in various provinces, as well as the provincial compulsory education experimental zones, should be opened at the beginning of the second year. The college recruits students who have completed the second year of university and gives them two terms of training. In the first term, they study at the school for one year and are then sent to various rural normal schools to serve as teachers. After serving for two years, they return to the school to study for another year, and are awarded a bachelor's degree, allowing them to serve as principals, teachers, and educational administrators in rural normal schools.

The rural normal specialized department is set up in the provincial rural normal college, recruits high school graduates, trains them for one year, gives them a certificate of completion, and sends them to serve as teachers and staff in central primary schools, members of rural education committees, or assistant teachers in rural normal schools. Afterwards, they must enroll in school for research every summer vacation. After completing three summer vacations, they can be awarded a diploma from the rural normal specialized department. The compulsory education experimental zones in various provinces should also be divided into urban and rural areas for students to practice and serve as the foundation for promoting compulsory education throughout the province.

Eleventh, the county or county-jointly established rural normal schools will be opened in three phases. From the third, fourth, and fifth years, one-third of them will be established separately. A total of 500 county-level normal schools and 500 urban and rural compulsory education experimental zones will be added nationwide each year from the third year to the fifth year.

County-level rural normal schools recruit junior high school graduates, study for two years, and send them to serve as teachers in rural primary schools. Afterwards, they must enroll in school every summer vacation. After completing three summer vacations, they are given a rural normal school diploma and are allowed to serve as teachers in central schools and educational administrators in various rural areas.

Rural normal schools can also recruit graduates from higher primary schools who are over 15 years old, study for three years, and send them to serve as assistant teachers in various rural primary schools. After serving for two years and completing two summer school sessions, they return to the school to study for one year, and then return to service to serve as rural primary school teachers. After another two years and completing two summer vacations, they can be awarded a formal normal school or high school normal department diploma and a central primary school teacher's license.

Twelfth, by the end of the fifth year, compulsory education teacher training institutions and compulsory education experimental zones in various provinces and cities will be widely established. From the sixth year onwards, together with existing provincial normal schools and newly established county-level rural normal schools, 90,000 teachers will be trained each year. After deducting 15,000 retired teachers, the net increase in teachers each year is 75,000. In this way, 75,000 new primary school classes can be added to educate 3 million children. By the eighteenth year, primary schools can be widely established throughout the country. By the twentieth year, a four-year compulsory education can be fully implemented nationwide.

In addition to running teacher training institutions at all levels, the following matters must be carried out:

A. Register all graduates of normal schools and normal training courses in the province, and advise them to go to various primary schools to serve. All normal school graduates who do not have jobs shall be assigned to various counties by the education department to serve as primary school teachers.

B. Strictly implement the service regulations for normal school graduates. Those who have received normal education must serve in primary schools for three to five years.

C. All teachers who have not graduated from formal normal schools shall be re-examined, and those who have qualified academic knowledge and experience shall be hired separately to make up for the shortage of teachers, and regulations on teacher summer vacation training shall be formulated and strictly implemented so that their academic knowledge can be improved at any time.

D. Primary school teachers who fail the examination shall be sent to the county-level rural normal schools for one or two years of training.

E. Examine private school teachers. Those who pass the examination shall be temporarily appointed as rural primary school teachers, and shall receive supplementary normal education during the summer vacation. Private school teachers who fail the examination shall be advised to attend county-level rural normal schools for more than two years of training.

(5) Ways to Increase Classrooms

To implement compulsory education, the country needs to add one million classrooms. The country has 1,915 counties, and each county needs to add an average of more than 500 classrooms. At present, there are financial difficulties, and local areas may not be able to build them specifically, so the following methods have to be adopted:

A. Use the family temples of the people across the country. The Chinese people are rich in family concepts, and the first family often has a family temple (or ancestral hall). The government can borrow a part of the family temple to run primary schools and at the same time bear the responsibility of repairing the family temple. Both sides have mutual benefits, and the people should welcome it. B. Use academic palaces, academies, and other common places. This matter has already been implemented in most places. There should be no opposition to using academic palaces, academies, and other places to run primary schools. C. Use all temples and monasteries. All temples and monasteries should allocate a part to the government to run primary schools. This is different from confiscating temple property, and it has fewer malpractices than monks and Taoists running primary schools themselves.

D. Encourage private donations of houses or donations to build school buildings. The villas built by the rich are often closed all year round, only for the accommodation of two or three caretakers. If they can donate or lend a part to run primary schools, it will be of great benefit to the government. The government should encourage and promote it, and give appropriate rewards. As for donating money to build school buildings, special rewards should be given.

E. The government should raise funds to build a kind of school building that is extremely economical and durable, and set a standard for simple and practical equipment for various places

to adopt. A part of the subsidies allocated by the central government and the national treasury should be used as the cost of building school buildings.

Roughly estimated, it costs at least 200 yuan to convert an old-style house into a classroom, and various equipment needed in each classroom also costs about 300 yuan. Therefore, each class costs a total of 500 yuan to open (to be continued).

Rice Prices Fall Again Yesterday

Since the Social Bureau severely cracked down on it, merchants who are blinded by greed have been wary and dare not engage in monopolistic behavior again. Therefore, the arrival of goods has improved day by day, and prices have gradually fallen. Yesterday, the price of Sutong White Rice in Nanshi fell back to 17.7 yuan, but no one paid attention. Songjiang Thin Rice opened at 17.5 yuan, and Liantang Thin Rice was at 17.12 yuan. Sales were also sluggish. The price of foreign rice remained firm due to the large number of exports, and it was difficult to fall back for a while. Yesterday, Saigon No. 1 opened at 15.2 yuan, and Xiaojiao was at 14.6 yuan. The buying sentiment in Beishi also subsided because most importers were watching the market fall. Yesterday, there were about 200 rice boats under the river. Due to the price limit of 18 yuan, travelers, innkeepers, and all parties were waiting and watching. And the stock of the shops is enough to meet sales for more than half a month, so there is no need to rush to buy. In general, the rice market in the north and south has eased, and prices will not rise, it is said.

(3) The county governor submitted for discussion the letter from the county party department requesting that the issue of funding for the district party department be submitted to the county government meeting for discussion and allocation (The resolution was) to reply to the county party department that it is difficult to subsidize the funding difficulties. (5) Omitted. (6) The Finance Bureau proposed that, according to the report of the collection officials, the township chiefs of the eighteenth year winter transport have not yet received the string to urge payment and how to handle it (The resolution was) to be submitted to the next district government meeting for discussion. The outline of the organization of the Shanghai County Literacy Movement Propaganda Conference is recorded below: (1) The name is the Shanghai County Literacy Movement Propaganda Conference. (2) Goals: (1) To arouse the need for literacy among the people of the county. (2) To understand the meaning of public education and be able to sympathize and cooperate. (3) To promote local autonomy through the literacy movement. (4) To focus on rural areas. (3) The committee shall be convened regularly by the county governor to organize the Literacy Movement Committee, with the county governor as chairman. (1) The County Party Department. (2) The Education Bureau (3) District Directors (4) Social Education Institutions (5) County Junior High Schools and Rural Normal Schools. (4) Branches: District Directors shall regularly convene the following personnel in each district to organize literacy movement branches, with the District Director as chairman. (1) District Party Department (2) Principals of each elementary school (3) Teachers of each public school (4) Township and town chiefs designated by the District Director (5) Various public organizations (such as farmers' associations and labor unions) (5) Organize the establishment of departments in the county general association of the literacy movement committee and the establishment of departments in the district branches. The organization is as follows: (1) The county general association has an editorial department, a publication department, a lecture department, a general affairs department, and an entertainment department. (2) Each district branch has a lecture department, a general affairs department, and an entertainment department. (6) Methods: The committee shall organize and complete the work on the specified date of the literacy movement, formulate methods, distribute them to each branch, and participate separately on the specified date. Each branch district shall organize and complete the preparations one week before the specified date. (7) Dates: May 20 for the first district, May 21 for the second district, May 22 for the third district, May 23 for the fourth district, May 24 for the fifth district, and May 25 for the sixth district. (8) Implementation: This charter shall be implemented after being passed by the county government meeting.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs Warns Township Chiefs 145

Must Not Exceed Authority and Violate the Law

Must Not Be Influenced by Officialdom

The Shanghai County Government received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, which stated that it had been learned that the heads and deputies of townships and towns in various counties often interfered in local civil and criminal litigation, and even issued tickets to summon people, hold court hearings, and arbitrarily impose large fines. They used notices and instructions for the people. Such illegal acts are detrimental to the progress of autonomy. It must be known that the heads and deputies of townships and towns are local autonomous personnel and are responsible for representing the provincial government to guide the people. They are completely different from the former clerks and gentry, so they must not exceed their authority and violate the law, and even more must not be influenced by officialdom. It is hereby ordered that the county governor shall comply with this order. If the heads and deputies of townships and towns commit the aforementioned acts again in the future, once reported, the district directors shall be allowed to investigate and report, and they will be severely punished without any leniency. County Governor Leng ordered all district directors to comply with the order yesterday.

Amendment to the Chamber of Commerce Law Approved by the Ministry

Executive and Supervisory Committee Member Quota Not Approved for Increase

The Chamber of Commerce previously stated that the number of executive and supervisory committee members stipulated by the Chamber of Commerce Law was too small to be sufficient for official duties, and submitted a request to the Ministry of Commerce for amendment. Now, approval No. 9157 from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has been received, acknowledging the presentation. Regarding point one in the presentation, concerning the number of executive committee members, the Chamber of Commerce Law does not adopt a sectoral representation system for executive and supervisory committee members. Their mission is to develop the overall interests with a unified force, which is different from the old Chamber of Commerce's board of directors system. Regarding point two, concerning the relationship between industrial and commercial guilds and the Chamber of Commerce, the industrial and commercial guilds are important components of the Chamber of Commerce. In principle, the Chamber of Commerce is generated by the guilds, so the Chamber does not adopt a Chamber of Commerce certification system. This matter concerns changing the legislative principle, and the requested forwarding is difficult to approve. According to the presentation, it should be noted accordingly.

International Labour Office Establishes Branch in China

Chen Zongcheng Appointed Director

The International Labour Office in Geneva, due to China's rising international status and the National Government's emphasis on protecting labor, decided this year to establish a branch in China to promote international cooperation in labor affairs. The branch address is approximately in Nanjing. Chen Zongcheng, Secretary of the International Labour Office, has been appointed as the branch director. Chen will soon return to China via Japan for preliminary investigations. It is expected he will arrive in Shanghai around the end of May. Chen holds a doctorate in political economy from the University of Paris and has served as secretary at the International Labour Office in Geneva, responsible for Chinese labor affairs, for five years. He accompanied Director Thomas of the International Labour Office on his visit to China two years ago and has been highly regarded by Thomas. His return to China to oversee the International Labour Office branch will contribute significantly to various issues between China and the international community.

Yangtze River Shipping News

Jiujiang Martial Law Reduces Cargo and Passengers. With the Communist Party rising up in Jiangxi Province, Jiujiang has declared martial law. Cargo from Jiangxi to Shanghai is mostly loaded onto ships from Xunpu, but since this month, no one dares to load cargo. Dockworkers have also stopped working together, resulting in a significant decrease in cargo from Jiujiang on downstream ships on the Yangtze River in recent days. Even passengers do not dare to take Chinese merchant ships east. Yesterday, when a Chinese merchant ship arrived in Shanghai, there were only five passengers from Jiujiang. It is said that commerce on the Nanxun Road has been halted by banditry, and people in Xunpu have been slightly more stable since the third day, but shipments from Shanghai, except for salt, have all decreased.

The Strike Wave is Gradually Expanding.

After the strike wave at the Chongqing Lingjiang Guild, foreign ships are still insisting. The loading and unloading guild in Yichang has demanded an increase in wages and has proposed conditions that each piece of cargo, regardless of loading or unloading, originally paid 150 cash, should be increased to 300 cash from April. The reason is that copper coins are extremely cheap in Yichang, with each yuan falling to 4,600-4,700 cash. The shipping companies say that the cost of labor in Yichang is already high, with loading and unloading fees costing 40 taels of silver per hundred tons of cargo, which is three times more than the 14 taels per hundred tons in Shanghai. If it is increased again, it will become 80 taels per hundred tons. Therefore, the foreign merchants have agreed to refuse, and the barge and dock gangs in the port have risen up to support the loading and unloading gang, and the strike wave is expanding. Yesterday, the Shanghai shipping industry received a telegram from Yichang saying that the shipping industry union has come forward to mediate, hoping to avoid disrupting transportation. The results are still unknown. The Yichang Municipal Party Department has taken advantage of the suspension of foreign ships to pressure Chinese Lingjiang, and has issued a declaration to quickly recover the navigation rights of the Sichuan River.

Chinese Jiang Ships Released to Shanghai One After Another.

Headquarters Traffic Department, in response to the request of Shanghai shipping merchants, is gradually releasing the Jiang ships back to Shanghai. The Minghe of Sanbei can also arrive in Shanghai today. The ships released and operating include Jiangxin, Jiangshun, Jianghua, Jiang'an, Jianguo, Jiangyu, Jiangjing, Ningshao, Yongxing, Xinningxing, and Minghe, a total of eleven ships.

Key News on North-South Shipping

Prohibition of Coffins, Reduction of Shifts, Prevention of Theft

Coffins Prohibited from Being Transported to Guangdong. Yesterday, a local shipping company received a telegram from Guangzhou stating that the Guangdong authorities have decided that coffins are prohibited from being imported from today onwards. Shanghai-bound ships to Guangdong have been ordered to stop accepting coffins for transport to Guangdong to avoid being blocked from landing or having the coffins opened for inspection in Guangdong. After receiving the telegram, a certain foreign ship took the lead in implementing the measure, and several coffins were blocked at the pier and could not be loaded.

Tianjin Foreign Ships Reduce Shifts. Since the traffic on the Jinpu Railway was interrupted and customers in North China stopped shipping goods, Shanghai's North Sea ships have been greatly affected. The number of goods shipped to Tianjin has decreased daily. Taikoo Company in Shanghai, in the Tianjin route, in addition to the three regular ships that still operate to carry passengers, the six or seven Tianjin cargo ships have completely stopped sailing to Tianjin and have changed their route to Niuzhuang and Dalian.

Shipping Merchants' Anti-Theft Meeting. In recent years, almost all of the north-south ships of various shipping companies in Shanghai have been robbed by pirates in Dapeng Bay. Now, in order to ensure the safety of navigation, various shipping companies, including British Taikoo and Jardine Matheson, have specifically consulted with the Chinese Navy to form an anti-theft committee to discuss the fundamental plan for suppressing pirates in the South China Sea and the arrangement for anti-theft on ships. The committee is located in Hong Kong. More than a dozen shipping companies operating on the South China routes in Shanghai have applied to join in recent days.

National Goods Association Requests Reduced Tax Rate on Zhongshan Ge

The China National Goods Maintenance Association requested the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to reduce the tax rate on Zhongshan Ge, stating, "We have recently received a letter from the Shengjing Silk Industry Association, a member of our association, stating that the Zhongshan Ge silk produced by our industry has recently been valued and taxed by the Shanghai Customs, amounting to as much as 18 or 19 taels of silver per load, which is higher than the tax rate on any other type of silk. As a result, sales have plummeted and business is difficult. In addition to our association submitting a request to the Ministry of Finance and Industry and Commerce to reduce the export tax on Zhongshan Ge, we specifically request your association to grant maintenance and provide sympathetic assistance to maintain national goods. We are deeply grateful, etc." According to this, we have learned that the Zhongshan Ge in question is made entirely of rayon and cotton, with no real silk mixed in. It is a purely imitation product. Since its launch, it has not only been able to slightly resist the invasion of foreign silk, but also supports the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of industrial and commercial people. National and economic interests benefit. It is noted that the export tax of the Customs stipulates that silk and rayon interweaves, or silk and cotton interweaves, are subject to a unified tax of only five taels and five qian of silver per load, while this Zhongshan Ge is purely a rayon and cotton interweave. Although the goods appear beautiful, the cost is very low. It should be taxed at half the rate to comply with tax regulations. Even if we take a step back and tax it at the rate of five taels and five qian, merchants already feel that the burden is too heavy and sales are difficult. However, the Jianghai Customs regards it as a new product and arbitrarily increases the tax, sometimes without standards, raising the valuation, resulting in a tax payment exceeding the cost by as much as 18 or 19 taels per load. As the tax rate increases, the cost naturally increases, coupled with the layering of fees and demands from officials, what crime have merchants committed to suffer such poisoning? It is no wonder that foreign goods are taxed once and sold everywhere, flooding the country, leaking hundreds of millions, and exhausting the country and impoverishing the people. Now that our National Government is recovering tariff autonomy and implementing it, the actions of the Customs have a great impact. Moreover, at a time when the national silk industry is declining, we should be united, work hard to promote it, reduce the tax amount, and expand foreign sales, so that we can save the industry and prevent leaks. Our association is based on the future of national goods, so we dare to report on the situation on its behalf, and we implore your department to order the Jianghai Customs to reduce the tax rate on this item and not exceed the tax rate of five taels and five qian per load of silk and rayon or cotton interweaves. We implore you to understand the difficulties and allow the promotion of sales, so as to maintain national goods and protect industry and commerce. We cannot bear the urgency to wait for orders. Standing Committee Members of the China National Goods Maintenance Association, Wang Jiean, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqiang, kowtow together.

Local News

Xie Baosheng's Son Escapes from Bandit Boat in Sanhuangni Creek

---A Total of Eleven People Have Been Captured---

Distant Relatives Come to Shanghai, Offering Diligence

Negotiations Reveal Flaws

Xie Baosheng Personally Takes Action

Rescuing His Beloved Son, Not Avoiding Hardship

On the evening of the 22nd of last month, the home of Li Mingzhai at No. 817 Qunshou Lane, White Rock Road, was burgled by armed robbers. Ornaments worth thousands of dollars were stolen, and his seven-year-old nephew, Xie Songtao, was kidnapped. Xie is the young son of Xie Baosheng, the current comprador of the China Merchants Bureau's Xinming Steamship. Details have already been recorded in this newspaper. It is now heard that the hostage, Xie Songtao, was released yesterday morning after being detained on the bandit boat for about seventeen days. The details of the kidnappers' contact and the cracking of the case obtained by this newspaper are recorded in sections below.

The Kidnappers Pretend to Visit

Since Xie Songtao was kidnapped, his biological mother, Li, has been extremely worried. Having a pearl snatched from her palm, she is heartbroken all day long. His father, Baosheng, is alert and once served as the captain of the detective team of the former Public Security Bureau. He paid attention to the clues of the case early on. However, the bandits did not make any contact or send any letters. Besides strict investigation, there was little chance of cracking the case. Unexpectedly, on the 30th of last month, a distant relative of Li, Peng Yuansheng, from Yancheng, who is forty-four years old, came, claiming to inquire about the kidnapping. In his words, he emphasized that contact must be made as soon as possible to get the pearl back. Li did not notice and, thinking he had good intentions, entrusted him with the task of contact.

Entrusting Someone to Negotiate in Changzhou

Xie Li was anxious to get her son back as soon as possible. Therefore, Peng Yuansheng came to her home the next day. Considering that he was a distant relative from the same hometown and willing to take on this arduous task, she was overjoyed. She did not know that Peng was one of the bandits. He claimed that the hostage was hidden in the Changzhou area based on reports from his friends. Xie's intention was not to make secret contact. However, now that Peng Yuansheng had come, there must be clues. Moreover, since he was a fellow townsman who had not been in contact this year, she was quite suspicious. Therefore, she paid him six silver dollars and asked him to go to Changzhou. If the bandits had a flexible solution, it would be best. Otherwise, she would publish a statement in the newspaper, not pursuing the matter further.

Flaws Revealed in the Letter

After receiving the commission from Xie's house, Peng Yuansheng went to Changzhou to negotiate the ransom. Unexpectedly, he did not return for several days. Xie thought that it would only take a day to travel back and forth between Changzhou and Shanghai. Why did Peng Yuansheng not come back after going? There must be other circumstances. Until the morning of April, a letter came from the bandits, with an overbearing tone, demanding 50,000 yuan and requiring the money to be paid within five days, otherwise the hostage would be killed. Xie ignored it because there was no contact address. However, on the same afternoon, another letter came from the bandits with a similar tone, but they forbade publishing in the newspaper, saying that even millions in cash would not be accepted if such an announcement was published. Xie thought that only three people knew about the newspaper publication. Now that the kidnappers were using this to threaten her, Peng Yuansheng's suspicion became more apparent.

The Principal Interrogates the Origin of the Weapons

At noon on the fifth day, Peng Yuansheng, who was said to have gone to Changzhou for talks, suddenly arrived. After meeting with Li, he talked a lot about how hard he worked in Changzhou, but he was detained by bandits at No. 3 Changxing Hotel in Changzhou for a disagreement. Li learned of this and, because this was a big matter, she informed the old house at No. 5 Fufu Lane, Edward Road, by telephone, instructing Xie Baosheng to come in person. After Xie received the call, he drove there. Seeing Peng's unusual expression, he questioned him in every possible way. Peng was uneasy. However, Xie was a well-known figure in the exploration area. Seeing this situation, he was about to report the arrest. It happened that the special investigators of the General Patrol House had received a secret report, saying that contacting the bandits was suspected of being a major crime. Therefore, they sent Chinese and Western detectives to arrest Peng Yuansheng at the address.

Five People Captured at Night

The Chinese and Western detectives of the General Investigation Department of the General Patrol House brought Peng Yuansheng back to the patrol house, believing that he was highly suspicious. After strict interrogation, Peng began to admit that he was the same party as the kidnappers. The detectives then took Peng to the address at No. 239 Luban Road, French Concession, to point out the arrest. They arrested Yang Denge and Yang Xuesheng, two people from Jiangbei. They also sent several detectives to stay in the house. At ten o'clock that night, the bandit gang Zhang Wansheng, Feng Yuanxue, and Li Ganquan returned to their nest from outside and were also captured. A total of five people were arrested. Yang Denge then confessed that Peng Yuansheng instructed him to prepare a small boat for moving, but he did not expect to kidnap the hostage. He did not know. The detectives asked where the boat was parked. Yang said that it was near the Damu Bridge in Rihui Port.

Strict Inspection of Ships in the Port

After obtaining the confession, the detectives of the Patrol House used an official document to submit it to Yuan Liang, the Director of the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau, because the hostage was hidden in the Chinese界. After hearing the news, Yuan immediately ordered Xu Jishi, the captain of the Water Patrol Team, to supervise Patrol Officer Li Chenghua, Patrol Leader Wu Minshen, Detective Liu Changrui, Ma Ruyun, Zhang Yuting, Yang Chunting, Jiang Linquan, etc., to meet with the Chinese and Western detectives of the Public Concession Patrol House and the victim Xie Baosheng, each with flashlights, guns, and weapons. They secretly went to the Suzhou River, Rihui Port, and Hongqiao area to check the parked ships. The detectives searched strictly for half a day, but there were no results. Fortunately, a tip came that a boat was parked in Huangni Creek, Qibao Town, Qingpu County, which was very suspicious.

The Hostage Bandit Ship Was Discovered

Until about 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, at a distance of nine miles from Qibao Town, a place called Huangni Creek, on the north side of the river, a small northeastern boat was found parked there. However, after inspecting the boat, there was a foul smell everywhere, making people want to vomit. Captain Xu and the detectives of the Patrol House immediately boarded the ship to conduct an inspection. In the front cabin of the ship, they saw two men sleeping soundly with their flashlights. A child was lying naked between the two men. At that time, Xie Baosheng identified the child under the light as his beloved son Songtao, who had been kidnapped for more than ten days and had not escaped. He was overjoyed on the spot. The detectives each held their guns and monitored the situation, preventing any accidents. Xie immediately embraced his son, but the child's body was very dirty and emaci

Telegram Regarding Reduction of Overseas Chinese Postal Rates 147

The National Federation of Overseas Chinese Associations, the National Federation of Commerce and Industry, and other groups telegraphed to various overseas Chinese organizations in Singapore yesterday, stating that the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce, various organizations in Singapore petitioning for reduced overseas Chinese postal rates, the Overseas Chinese Congress, the Shantou General Chamber of Commerce, the Shantou Wholesale Association, the Xiamen General Chamber of Commerce, and the Xiamen Wholesale Association, all noted that the Ministry of Communications, Postal Administration, had initiated the cancellation of Overseas Chinese private postal agencies and increased postal rates. Our associations and others repeatedly telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Ministry of Communications, and the Construction Commission, requesting that the responsible officials of the Ministry of Communications be dismissed and that a nationwide announcement be made to all countries, so that overseas Chinese mail would continue to be charged according to the original rates for an indefinite extension. After the implementation of the Universal Postal Convention, we received a letter from the Government Secretariat stating that the Ministry of Communications had replied, according to a report from the Postal Administration, after receiving a telegram from the Kuala Lumpur Postal Administration, stating that the Kuala Lumpur Postal Administration had not declared to overseas Chinese representatives that this case was initiated by the Chinese government, etc. We telegraphed the government again, pointing out that the Postal Administration did not inquire with the Singapore government, but instead inquired with the Kuala Lumpur post office, which was clearly an attempt to evade the truth, and requested that the postal rate increase be cancelled. We also organized a joint conference to fight for the overseas Chinese postal rate increase, and elected Chen Zhiying, Xu Jigong, Chen Chunan, Zheng Qizhong, Lin Jingqian, Zhu Xiajiu, and Zhuo Wuchu as seven general representatives to handle this matter. At the second meeting on April 4th, we also invited Lin Shi, the general manager of the Postal Administration, to attend the meeting to explain the process. On that day, General Affairs Section Chief Yu Xianglin and Committee Member Xu Yingsan were sent by General Manager Lin to report that a telegram had been received from the Ministry of Communications, approving a reduction in postal rates for domestic mail to Southeast Asia to five cents per twenty grams, and a public letter was enclosed stating that the request from your association to ban Overseas Chinese private postal agencies was approved, and a telegram should be sent to the Shantou and Xiamen post offices to postpone implementation. After investigating this case, it was found that it was a request from the British Malaya Kuala Lumpur post office and the handling of the situation by our office had been communicated previously. Later, a letter was received from the British post office, stating that it would be implemented after March 31st according to Universal Postal Convention rates. Due to the urgency of the situation, we were concerned that our national postal agencies' general packages to Southeast Asia would be penalized for not complying with Universal Postal Convention rates, so we telegraphed the British post office to extend the deadline and reported to the ministry for instructions. We then received a reply by telegram from the British Malaya Kuala Lumpur post office, stating that private postal agency mail from China to Southeast Asia before May 1st would not be treated as underpaid mail. Now, we have received another telegram from the Ministry of Communications stating that the British post office requests an increase in fees for mail from private postal agencies in Southeast Asia. After repeated appeals from overseas Chinese organizations, the Ministry, understanding the situation and knowing that overseas Chinese are facing genuine difficulties, decided to make appropriate accommodations in consideration of the feelings of overseas Chinese. In the future, mail sent from private postal agencies to British Malaya should be charged five cents per letter per twenty grams to show consideration and comfort to overseas Chinese. The British Malaya post office has already been contacted for serious consultation and decision. Based on current market prices, five cents in Chinese silver currency is less than three cents in the currency commonly used in the British Malaya islands. It can be seen here that the Chinese government is sympathetic to the difficulties of overseas Chinese. We will report further after receiving a reply telegram, and we are sending this letter to inform you for your reference. After investigating, our associations originally intended to firmly request the cancellation of the postal rate increase plan, but since the five cents per letter postage for domestic mail and six cents per letter postage for foreign mail were requested by Mr. Li Weinan, Chairman of the Singapore Overseas Chinese Congress, it was not appropriate to argue too much. According to the above-mentioned letter, we are sending this telegram to inform you for your reference. Furthermore, since private postal agencies do not comply with the Universal Postal Convention, the national Postal Administration has established special rules for postal consignment agencies, charging two yuan for the signboard and one yuan per year for the license. This does not violate the Universal Postal Convention and can provide convenience for private postal agencies. General Affairs Section Chief Yu requested to be informed of these details. We also request the Shantou and Xiamen General Chambers of Commerce to inform the Wholesale Associations to follow suit. The rules for special postal consignment agencies are attached. Sincerely, the National Federation of Overseas Chinese Associations, the National Federation of Commerce and Industry, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Promotion Association, Jinan University, the Southeast Asia Cultural Department, and the Southeast Asia Students Association.

Popularity of Woolen Fabrics on This Street 148

Diminished Interest from Customer Groups

Recently, stores selling woolen goods, new clothing stores, and hat and shoe workshops on this street have shown strong interest in woolen fabrics. As the weather warms, actual sales are starting to pick up, and small-scale retail transactions have also suddenly increased. There is continued demand for serge, worsted, fancy suiting, flannel, summer fabrics, etc., and wholesale orders are being placed for both individual pieces and entire boxes. Blue continues to be the popular color for serge. Only Shui Mei's Dujian brand of raincoat fabric continues to be popular, with the Ningfeng, Xinji, Rongtai, and Taili brands all selling for three taels and five qian and a half. Recently, customer groups have shown less interest, especially those from the north. Currently, only the large and small Sichuan customer groups still have demand. Other small inland customer groups also have a decent business in piecemeal wholesale and selling by the piece.

Silk and Tea: Weakening Old Cocoons 149

Total Shanghai Factory Customers Under 40,000

No Improvement in Silk Sales by Foreign Firms: The Qingming Festival has passed, and farmers in the interior are all preparing to incubate silkworm eggs. Last year's silkworm cocoon harvest was poor, and there was already a shortage for reeling. The stock of old cocoons in Shanghai warehouses is becoming increasingly scarce. Due to the current unrest, the existing cocoons in the Yangtze River area are all being loaded onto ships and transported to Shanghai to be sold while the opportunity exists. However, the quantity is limited. An investigation shows that the total number of cocoons held by various foreign firms and factories, together with the newly transported cocoons from Anhui and Hubei, is less than 40,000 bales. If all the silk factories in Shanghai were to resume operations, it would still be difficult to sustain production. Yesterday, silk sales by foreign firms in Shanghai showed no improvement. The foreign exchange rate was unstable, and telegrams were quiet. Only Dachang and others imported 40 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, Xin Shichang and others imported 15 bales of Qian Da silk, and Kechang imported 9 bales of coarse yellow silk. Prices remain firm.

Flourishing Hardware and French Nails 150

French nails are thriving. Previously, the trade in French nails was pessimistic because the nails could be exported with a complete exemption from half the tax, which caused an unusually pessimistic trend and gave the market an outwardly strong but inwardly weak appearance. In recent days, according to news from the customs authorities, exports are no longer permitted, so the business of imported goods is flourishing. The number of forward contracts being unloaded is increasing. As a result, market prices are rising steadily. Currently, ordinary patterns can be opened to six taels and six qian, and better patterns are priced at six taels and seven or eight qian. According to a tea party investigation, a total of two or three thousand barrels were loaded for export yesterday, and another 2,500 barrels are awaiting shipment to Wuhan today.

The Paris Grand Theater announced that "The Secret Room Gunfire" is a masterpiece starring the new stars George Meek and Majiao Pipi. The plot is strange, mysterious, and unpredictable, with many mechanisms and incredible transformations. It is one of the treasures of the Fox Film Corporation's silent films and will be screened at our theater starting today.

Calligraphy and Painting News 155

The famous painter Wang Jiyuan is about to travel to Europe and has scheduled a personal painting exhibition and appraisal meeting at the Ningbo Association on Xizang Road from April 10th to 14th. More than one hundred of Wang's creations, including Chinese paintings and Western paintings, with innovative spirit, will be displayed. The opening is sure to be a grand occasion. Lu Gongwang of Beijing previously held a 10% discount for the spring season and waived the ink fee for one month to build relationships with customers. In recent days, many works have been received. Major stationery stores both in and outside Shanghai are representatives. The general receiving address is 129 Pierre le Grand Road, French Concession. The price list will be sent upon request.

Page 22

Social News

Japanese Doll Festival 156

March 3rd is the Japanese girls' Doll Festival, called "Hina Matsuri" in Japanese. Families with daughters must clean and decorate a room on this day, setting up an altar covered with silk and brocade, and placing foreign dolls on it, so that their lovely daughters can offer cakes and worship. This year, it was held again as usual, creating a lively atmosphere. It is also known as the Peach Blossom Festival because it falls during the sunny weather when peach blossoms are in full bloom.

The Story of the Doll Festival 157

Legend has it that in a village in ancient China, there were three beautiful and intelligent young women who suddenly passed away on March 3rd. People considered this day unlucky for girls, so they began to make dolls and throw them into the turbid river on that day, hoping that the dolls would carry away the bad luck of the daughters. This practice does not seem to be heard of or practiced in our country, but it has been a traditional custom in Japan for over a thousand years. However, the rituals are slightly different, and the practice of throwing them into the turbid river is not adopted.

The Doll Festival in the Palace 158

The Japanese Emperor has two princesses, Princess Teru and Princess Taka. This year, American girls raised funds to purchase hundreds of dolls for the two princesses to celebrate the festival and to strengthen the friendly feelings between the girls of the two countries. At the same time, Dr. Sheltner's book "Loving Dolls" was sent to the noble girls. Therefore, this year's festival was especially joyous. On this day, the palace was decorated extremely luxuriously and magnificently. The four walls were hung with silk and brocade depicting the above-mentioned story. The palace pillars were adorned with fresh flowers, and the fragrance was intoxicating. Thousands of silver lamps were placed on the ground. A large altar was set up in the center, covered with scarlet brocade. Sandalwood was burning on it. There were seven levels, and dolls were placed on them. Some wore ancient clothing, some were dressed fashionably, some were beautiful women with captivating eyes, some were heroic and awe-inspiring, and others were grotesque or had large bellies. Some were reaching out their hands as if begging, and some were naked and performing celestial devil dances. All kinds of dolls were available, making it difficult to describe them all. At 11:00 a.m., Princess Teru and Princess Taka attended the ceremony. Elegant music led the way, followed by lanterns. Princess Taka was young and could not walk on her own, so she was carried by a servant. Emperor Showa led the noble women to stand on the side of the hall to watch the ceremony. The Empress assisted Princess Teru in offering cakes, candies, and mochi (a type of Japanese cake), and offered wine three times, bowing and paying respects. The music in both corridors began to play, and palace maids danced with colored silks on the hall. The Empress carried the two princesses down, and the ceremony was completed. In the afternoon, the Emperor hosted a banquet to wish the two princesses good fortune. A joyful atmosphere filled the palace.

The Doll Festival Among the People 159

On this day, every household in the country celebrates, with Tokyo being the most grand. In addition to private celebrations, there are also public celebrations. Hibiya Park and the competition ground are decorated in the most luxurious way. There is a doll exhibition and a doll theater. In the afternoon, schoolgirls perform various plays about dolls, as well as sing and dance. Over a thousand girls attend, and they all receive candies and other gifts, enjoying themselves immensely. At night, the Osaka Radio Station broadcasts a speech by Japanese artist Nishizawa, titled "The Literary Doll Festival," and a performance of "The Story of the Doll" by Ms. Ota to entertain girls throughout the country. (By Dui)

70,000 Danish Children Commemorate Andersen 160

Hans Christian Andersen's fairy tales are world-famous. Almost every country with written language has a translation of Andersen's fairy tales. April 2nd is the 125th anniversary of his birth. Over 70,000 Danish children have come together to commemorate this great poet.

Their method of commemoration is to choose the most interesting scenes from Andersen's fairy tales and dress up as described in the stories and parade on the streets. At that time, many residents and shops in Copenhagen (the capital of Denmark) raised flags to express their respect and enthusiasm for Andersen. These many innocent and cheerful children marched to the City Hall, where the mayor gave them a sincere speech. After the performance, everyone sang the national anthem and dispersed excitedly. This was the joy of the elementary school students. Some of the older students performed plays in schools, and some sang at home. That kind of festive atmosphere was more enthusiastic than any gathering. This also shows the appeal of Andersen's fairy tales. (By Mo)
